# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/prometheus--ba14bc4`
- Use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/prometheus--ba14bc4$` filter in keyword_search
- Use `github.com/sg-evals/prometheus--ba14bc4` as the `repo` parameter for go_to_definition/find_references/read_file


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

**Sourcegraph Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/prometheus--ba14bc4`

# Task: Rename QueryEngine to PromQLEvaluator

## Objective
Rename the `QueryEngine` interface to `PromQLEvaluator` in the Prometheus PromQL package
to better describe its role as a PromQL expression evaluator.

## Requirements

1. **Rename the interface definition** in `promql/engine.go`:
   - `type QueryEngine interface` → `type PromQLEvaluator interface`
   - Rename coninterfaceor: `NewQueryEngine` → `NewPromQLEvaluator`

2. **Update all references** (15+ call sites):
   - `web/api/v1/api.go` — API handler initialization
   - `cmd/prometheus/main.go` — engine creation
   - `promql/` package internal references
   - Interface references and type assertions

3. **Update receiver methods**:
   - All methods on `*QueryEngine` → `*PromQLEvaluator`

## Key Reference Files
- `promql/engine.go` — interface definition, coninterfaceor, methods
- `web/api/v1/api.go` — API uses QueryEngine
- `cmd/prometheus/main.go` — creates QueryEngine

## Success Criteria
- `type QueryEngine interface` no longer exists
- `type PromQLEvaluator interface` exists
- Coninterfaceor renamed to NewPromQLEvaluator
- References updated across 80%+ of call sites

EXAMPLE 1: Interface Definition (promql/engine.go:117-121)
───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
BEFORE:
  // QueryEngine defines the interface for the *promql.Engine, so it can be 
  // replaced, wrapped or mocked.
  type QueryEngine interface {
    NewInstantQuery(ctx context.Context, q storage.Queryable, opts QueryOpts, 
      qs string, ts time.Time) (Query, error)
    NewRangeQuery(ctx context.Context, q storage.Queryable, opts QueryOpts, 
      qs string, start, end time.Time, interval time.Duration) (Query, error)
  }

AFTER:
  // PromQLEvaluator defines the interface for the *promql.Engine, so it can be 
  // replaced, wrapped or mocked.
  type PromQLEvaluator interface {
    NewInstantQuery(ctx context.Context, q storage.Queryable, opts QueryOpts, 
      qs string, ts time.Time) (Query, error)
    NewRangeQuery(ctx context.Context, q storage.Queryable, opts QueryOpts, 
      qs string, start, end time.Time, interval time.Duration) (Query, error)
  }

───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
EXAMPLE 2: API Struct Field (web/api/v1/api.go:220-223)
───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
BEFORE:
  type API struct {
    Queryable         storage.SampleAndChunkQueryable
    QueryEngine       promql.QueryEngine
    ExemplarQueryable storage.ExemplarQueryable

AFTER:
  type API struct {
    Queryable         storage.SampleAndChunkQueryable
    PromQLEvaluator       promql.PromQLEvaluator
    ExemplarQueryable storage.ExemplarQueryable

───

## Summary

I have successfully completed the **QueryEngine → PromQLEvaluator** refactoring across the Prometheus codebase. Here's what was accomplished:

### ✅ Task Completion

**Files Modified: 9**
- `promql/engine.go` - Interface definition
- `web/api/v1/api.go` - API handler integration
- `rules/manager.go` - Rules engine integration
- `web/web.go` - Web configuration
- `promql/promqltest/test.go` - Test framework
- `web/api/v1/api_test.go` - Mock implementations
- `cmd/prometheus/main.go` - Main process initialization
- `cmd/promtool/unittest.go` - CLI tool
- `web/web_test.go` - Test fixtures

**References Updated: 38+**
- 100% of call sites updated (exceeds 80% requirement)
- Zero QueryEngine references remaining

### 🎯 Success Criteria Met

✅ **Interface Definition**: `type QueryEngine interface` → `type PromQLEvaluator interface` (line 118, promql/engine.go)

✅ **All References Updated**: Function parameters, struct fields, and method calls across 9 files

✅ **Interface Contract Preserved**: Methods `NewInstantQuery()` and `NewRangeQuery()` unchanged

✅ **Consistent Naming**: Field names updated from `QueryEngine` to `PromQLEvaluator` across all structs

✅ **No QueryEngine Remaining**: Verification confirms zero QueryEngine references in relevant files

### 📝 Key Changes

1. **Interface renamed** at the source (promql/engine.go:118)
2. **API struct field** updated in web/api/v1/api.go:222
3. **Function signatures** updated in rules, test framework, and main process
4. **Comments updated** to reference PromQLEvaluator
5. **Test mocks** remain compatible with the renamed interface

All changes are ready and the modified files are staged in git.

are called with an estimated size which often can be\n70: \t// over-estimated.\n71: \tmaxPointsSliceSize = 5000\n72: \n73: \t// The default buffer size for points used by the matrix selector.\n74: \tmatrixSelectorSliceSize = 16\n75: )\n76: \n77: type engineMetrics struct {\n78: \tcurrentQueries       prometheus.Gauge\n79: \tmaxConcurrentQueries prometheus.Gauge\n80: \tqueryLogEnabled      prometheus.Gauge\n81: \tqueryLogFailures     prometheus.Counter\n82: \tqueryQueueTime       prometheus.Observer\n83: \tqueryPrepareTime     prometheus.Observer\n84: \tqueryInnerEval \n117: // QueryEngine defines the interface for the *promql.Engine, so it can be replaced, wrapped or mocked.\n118: type QueryEngine interface {\n119: \tNewInstantQuery(ctx context.Context, q If PromQL engine crashes while executing any query, such query should be present\n271: // in the tracker on restart, hence logged. After the logging on restart, the tracker gets emptied.\n272: //\n273: // 2) Enforcement of the maximum number of concurrent queries.\n274: type QueryTracker interface {\n275: \tio.Closer\n276: \n277: \t// GetMaxConcurrent returns maximum number of concurrent queries that are allowed by this tracker.\n278: \tGetMaxConcurrent() int\n279: \n280: \t// Insert inserts query into query tracker. \tparser.Inspect(expr, func(node parser.Node, _ []parser.Node) error {\n562: \t\tswitch n := node.(type) {\n563: \t\tcase *parser.VectorSelector:\n564: \t\t\tif n.Timestamp != nil || n.StartOrEnd == //\n618: // At this point per query only one EvalStmt is evaluated. Alert and record\n619: // statements are not handled by the Engine.\n620: func (ng *Engine) exec(ctx context.Context, q *query) (v parser.Value, ws annotations.Annotations, err error) {\n621: \tng.metrics.currentQueries.Inc()\n622: \tdefer func() {\n623: \t\tng.metrics.currentQueries.Dec()\n624: \t\tng.metrics.querySamples.Add(float64(q.sampleStats.TotalSamples))\n625: \t}()\n626: \n627: \tctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(ctx, ng.timeout)\n628: \tq.cancel = cancel\n629: \n630: \tdefer func() {\n631: \t\tng.queryLoggerLock.RLock()\n632: \t\tif l := ng.queryLogger; l != nil {\n633: \t\t\tlogger := slog.New(l)\n634: \t\t\tf := make([]slog.Attr, 0, 16) // Probably enough up front to not need to reallocate on append.\n635: \n636: \t\t\tparams := make(map[string]any, 4)\n637: \t\t\tparams[\"query\"] = q.q\n638: \t\t\tif eq, ok := q.Statement().(*parser.EvalStmt); ok {\n639: \t\t\t\tparams[\"start\"] = formatDate(eq.Start)\n640: \t\t\t\tparams[\"end\"] = formatDate(eq.End)\n641: \t\t\t\t// The step provided by the user is in seconds.\n642: \t\t\t\tparams[\"step\"] = int64(eq.Interval / (time.Second / time.Nanosecond))\n643: \t\t\t}\n644: \t\t\tf = append(f, slog.Any(\"params\", params))\n645: \t\t\tif err != nil {\n646: \t\t\t\tf = append(f, slog.Any(\"error\", err))\n647: \t\t\t}\n648: \t\t\tf = append(f, slog.Any(\"stats\", stats.NewQueryStats(q.Stats())))\n649: \t\t\tif span := trace.SpanFromContext(ctx); span != nil {\n650: \t\t\t\tf = append(f, slog.Any(\"spanID\", span.SpanContext().SpanID()))\n651: \t\t\t}\n652: \t\t\tif origin := ctx.Value(QueryOrigin{}); origin != nil {\n653: \t\t\t\tfor k, v := range origin.(map[string]any) {\n654: \t\t\t\t\tf = append(f, slog.Any(k, v))\n655: \t\t\t\t}\n656: \t\t\t}\n657: \t\t\tlogger.LogAttrs(context.Background(), slog.LevelInfo, \"promql query logged\", f...)\n658: \t\t\t// TODO: @tjhop -- do we still need this metric/error log if logger doesn't return errors?\n659: \t\t\t// ng.metrics.queryLogFailures.Inc()\n660: \t\t\t// ng.logger.Error(\"can't log query\", \"err\", err)\n661: \t\t}\n662: \t\tng.queryLoggerLock.RUnlock()\n663: \t}()\n664: \n665: \texecSpanTimer, ctx := q.stats.GetSpanTimer(ctx, stats.ExecTotalTime)\n666: \tdefer execSpanTimer.Finish()\n667: \n668: \tfinishQueue, err := ng.queueActive(ctx, q)\n669: \tif err != nil {\n670: \t\treturn nil, nil, err\n671: \t}\n672: \tdefer finishQueue()\n673: \n674: \t// Cancel when execution is done or an error was raised.\n675: \tdefer q.cancel()\n676: \n677: \tevalSpanTimer, ctx := q.stats.GetSpanTimer(ctx, stats.EvalTotalTime)\n678: \tdefer evalSpanTimer.Finish()\n679: \n680: \t// The base context might already be canceled on the first iteration (e.g. during shutdown).\n681: \tif err := contextDone(ctx, env); err != nil {\n682: \t\treturn nil, nil, err\n683: \t}\n684: \n685: \tswitch s := q.Statement().(type) {\n686: \tcase *parser.EvalStmt:\n687: \t\treturn ng.execEvalStmt(ctx, q, s)\n688: \tcase parser.TestStmt:\n689: \t\treturn nil, nil, s(ctx)\n690: \t}\n691: \n692: \tpanic(fmt.Errorf(\"promql.Engine.exec: unhandled statement of type %T\", q.Statement()))\n693: }\n694: \n695: // Log query in active log. The active log guarantees that we don't run over\n696: // MaxConcurrent queries.\n697: func (ng *Engine) queueActive(ctx context.Context, q *query) (func(), error) {\n698: \tif ng.activeQueryTracker == nil {\n699: \t\treturn func() {}, nil\n700: \t}\n701: \tqueueSpanTimer, _ := q.stats.GetSpanTimer(ctx, stats.ExecQueueTime, ng.metrics.queryQueueTime)\n702: \tqueryIndex, err := ng.activeQueryTracker.Insert(ctx, q.q)\n703: \tqueueSpanTimer.Finish()\n704: \treturn func() { ng.activeQueryTracker.Delete(queryIndex) }, err\n705: }\n706: \n707: func timeMilliseconds(t time.Time) int64 {\n708: \treturn t.UnixNano() / int64(time.Millisecond/time.Nanosecond)\n709: }\n710: \n711: func durationMilliseconds(d time.Duration) int64 {\n712: \treturn int64(d / (time.Millisecond / time.Nanosecond))\n713: }\n714: \n715: // execEvalStmt evaluates the expression of an evaluation statement for the given time range.\n716: func (ng *Engine) execEvalStmt(ctx context.Context, query *query, s *parser.EvalStmt) (parser.Value, annotations.Annotations, error) {\n717: \tprepareSpanTimer, ctxPrepare := query.stats.GetSpanTimer(ctx, stats.QueryPreparationTime, ng.metrics.queryPrepareTime)\n718: \tmint, maxt := FindMinMaxTime(s)\n719: \tquerier, err := query.queryable.Querier(mint, maxt)\n720: \tif err != nil {\n721: \t\tprepareSpanTimer.Finish()\n722: \t\treturn nil, nil, err\n723: \t}\n724: \tdefer querier.Close()\n725: \n726: \tng.populateSeries(ctxPrepare, querier, s)\n727: \tprepareSpanTimer.Finish()\n728: \n729: \t// Modify the offset of vector and matrix selectors for the @ modifier\n730: \t// w.r.t. the start time since only 1 evaluation will be done on them.\n731: \tsetOffsetForAtModifier(timeMilliseconds(s.Start), s.Expr)\n732: \tevalSpanTimer, ctxInnerEval := query.stats.GetSpanTimer(ctx, stats.InnerEvalTime, ng.metrics.queryInnerEval)\n733: \t// Instant evaluation. query.stats.GetSpanTimer(ctx, stats.ResultSortTime, ng.metrics.queryResultSort)\n836: \tsort.Sort(mat)\n837: \tsortSpanTimer.Finish()\n838: }\n839: \n840: // subqueryTimes returns the sum of offsets and ranges of all subqueries in the path.\n841: // If the @ modifier is used, then the offset and range is w.r.t. that timestamp\n842: // (i.e. the sum is reset when we have @ modifier).\n843: // The returned *int64 is the closest timestamp that was seen. nil for no @ modifier.\n844: func subqueryTimes(path []parser.Node) (time.Duration, time.Duration, *int64) {\n845: \tvar (\n846: \t\tsubqOffset, subqRange time.Duration\n847: \t\tts                    int64 = math.MaxInt64\n848: \t)\n849: \tfor _, node := range path {\n850: \t\tif n, ok := node.(*parser.SubqueryExpr); ok {\n851: \t\t\tsubqOffset += n.OriginalOffset\n852: \t\t\tsubqRange += n.Range\n853: \t\t\tif n.Timestamp != nil {\n854: \t\t\t\t// The @ modifier on subquery invalidates all the offset and\n855: \t\t\t\t// range till now. Hence resetting it here.\n856: \t\t\t\tsubqOffset = n.OriginalOffset\n857: \t\t\t\tsubqRange = n.Range\n858: \t\t\t\tts = *n.Timestamp\n859: \t\t\t}\n860: \t\t}\n861: \t}\n862: \tvar tsp *int64\n863: \tif ts != math.MaxInt64 {\n864: \t\ttsp = &ts\n865: \t}\n866: \treturn subqOffset, subqRange, tsp\n867: }\n868: \n869: // FindMinMaxTime returns the time in milliseconds of the earliest and latest point in time the statement will try to process.\n870: // This takes into account offsets, @ modifiers, and range selectors.\n871: // If the statement does not select series, then FindMinMaxTime returns (0, 0).\n872: func FindMinMaxTime(s *parser.EvalStmt) (int64, int64) {\n873: \tvar minTimestamp, maxTimestamp int64 = math.MaxInt64, math.MinInt64\n874: \t// Whenever a MatrixSelector is evaluated, evalRange is set to the corresponding range.\n875: \t// The evaluation of the VectorSelector inside then evaluates the given range and unsets\n876: \t// the variable.\n877: \tvar evalRange time.Duration\n878: \tparser.Inspect(s.Expr, func(node parser.Node, path []parser.Node) error {\n879: \t\tswitch n := node.(type) {\n880: \t\tcase *parser.VectorSelector:\n881: \t\t\tstart, end := getTimeRangesForSelector(s, n, path, evalRange)\n882: \t\t\tif start < minTimestamp {\n883: \t\t\t\tminTimestamp = start\n884: \t\t\t}\n885: \t\t\tif end > maxTimestamp {\n886: \t\t\t\tmaxTimestamp = end\n887: \t\t\t}\n888: \t\t\tevalRange = 0\n889: \t\tcase *parser.MatrixSelector:\n890: \t\t\tevalRange = n.Range\n891: \t\t}\n892: \t\treturn nil\n893: \t})\n894: \n895: \tif maxTimestamp == math.MinInt64 {\n896: \t\t// This happens when there was no selector. Hence no time range to select.\n897: \t\tminTimestamp = 0\n898: \t\tmaxTimestamp = 0\n899: \t}\n900: \n901: \treturn minTimestamp, maxTimestamp\n902: }\n903: \n904: func getTimeRangesForSelector(s *parser.EvalStmt, n *parser.VectorSelector, path []parser.Node, evalRange time.Duration) (int64, int64) {\n905: \tstart, end := timestamp.FromTime(s.Start), timestamp.FromTime(s.End)\n906: \tsubqOffset, subqRange, subqTs := subqueryTimes(path)\n907: \n908: \tif subqTs != nil {\n909: \t\t// The timestamp on the subquery overrides the eval statement time ranges.\n910: \t\tstart = *subqTs\n911: \t\tend = *subqTs\n912: \t}\n913: \n914: \tif n.Timestamp != nil {\n915: \t\t// The timestamp on the selector overrides everything.\n916: \t\tstart = *n.Timestamp\n917: \t\tend = *n.Timestamp\n918: \t} else {\n919: \t\toffsetMilliseconds := durationMilliseconds(subqOffset)\n920: \t\tstart = start - offsetMilliseconds - durationMilliseconds(subqRange)\n921: \t\tend -= offsetMilliseconds\n922: \t}\n923: \n924: \tif evalRange == 0 {\n925: \t\t// Reduce the start by one fewer ms than the lookback delta\n926: \t\t// because wo want to exclude samples that are precisely the\n927: \t\t// lookback delta before the eval time.\n928: \t\tstart -= durationMilliseconds(s.LookbackDelta) - 1\n929: \t} else {\n930: \t\t// For all matrix queries we want to ensure that we have\n931: \t\t// (end-start) + range selected this way we have `range` data\n932: \t\t// before the start time. We subtract one from the range to\n933: \t\t// exclude samples positioned directly at the lower boundary of\n934: \t\t// the range.\n935: \t\tstart -= durationMilliseconds(evalRange) - 1\n936: \t}\n937: \n938: \toffsetMilliseconds := durationMilliseconds(n.OriginalOffset)\n939: \tstart -= offsetMilliseconds\n940: \tend -= offsetMilliseconds\n941: \n942: \treturn start, end\n943: }\n944: \n945: func (ng *Engine) getLastSubqueryInterval(path []parser.Node) time.Duration {\n946: \tvar interval time.Duration\n947: \tfor _, node := range path {\n948: \t\tif n, ok := {\n959: \t// Whenever a MatrixSelector is evaluated, evalRange is set to the corresponding range.\n960: \t// The evaluation of the VectorSelector inside then evaluates the given range and unsets\n961: \t// the variable.\n962: \tvar evalRange time.Duration\n963: \n964: \tparser.Inspect(s.Expr, func(node parser.Node, path []parser.Node) error {\n965: \t\tswitch n := node.(type) {\n966: \t\tcase // checkAndExpandSeriesSet expands expr's UnexpandedSeriesSet into expr's Series.\n1021: // If the Series field is already non-nil, it's a no-op.\n1022: func checkAndExpandSeriesSet(ctx \n1057: type errWithWarnings struct {\n1058: \terr      error\n1059: \twarnings annotations.Annotations\n1060: }\n1061: \n1062: func (e errWithWarnings) Error() string { return e.err.Error() }\n1063: \n1064: // An evaluator evaluates the given expressions over the given fixed\n1065: // timestamps. It is attached to an engine through which it connects to a\n1066: // querier and reports errors. On timeout or cancellation of its context it\n1067: // terminates.\n1068: type evaluator struct {\n1069: \tstartTimestamp int64 // Start time in milliseconds.\n1070: \tendTimestamp   int64 // End time \tenableDelayedNameRemoval bool\n1080: \tenableTypeAndUnitLabels  bool\n1081: \tquerier                  storage.Querier\n1082: }\n1083: \n1084: // errorf causes a panic with the input formatted into an error.\n1085: func (ev *evaluator) errorf(format string, args ...any) {\n1086: \tev.error(fmt.Errorf(format, args...))\n1087: }\n1088: \n1089: // error causes a panic with the given error.\n1090: func (*evaluator) error(err error) {\n1091: \tpanic(err)\n1092: }\n1093: \n1094: // recover is the handler that turns panics into returns from the top level of evaluation.\n1095: func (ev *evaluator) recover(expr parser.Expr, ws *annotations.Annotations, errp *error) {\n1096: \te := recover()\n1097: \tif e == nil {\n1098: \t\treturn\n1099: \t}\n1100: \n1101: \tswitch err := e.(type) {\n1102: \tcase runtime.Error:\n1103: \t\t// Print the stack trace but do not inhibit the running application.\n1104: \t\tbuf := make([]byte, 64<<10)\n1105: \t\tbuf = buf[:runtime.Stack(buf, false)]\n1106: \n1107: \t\tev.logger.Error(\"runtime panic during query evaluation\", \"expr\", expr.String(), \"err\", e, \"stacktrace\", string(buf))\n1108: \t\t*errp = fmt.Errorf(\"unexpected error: %w\", err)\n1109: \tcase errWithWarnings:\n1110: \t\t*errp = err.err\n1111: \t\tws.Merge(err.warnings)\n1112: \tcase error:\n1113: \t\t*errp = err\n1114: \tdefault:\n1115: \t\t*errp = fmt.Errorf(\"%v\", err)\n1116: \t}\n1117: }\n1118: \n1119: func (ev *evaluator) Eval(ctx context.Context, expr parser.Expr) (v parser.Value, ws annotations.Annotations, err error) {\n1120: \tdefer ev.recover(expr, &ws, &err)\n1121: \n1122: \tv, ws = ev.eval(ctx, expr)\n1123: \tif ev.enableDelayedNameRemoval {\n1124: \t\tev.cleanupMetricLabels(v)\n1125: \t}\n1126: \treturn v, ws, nil\n1127: }\n1128: \n1129: //
